                               Annex 10.3. ThePestManagementPlan

1.PESTMANAGEMENTSTRATEGY
In the second phase Project of the APL program and according to the environmental assessment
conducted, the Bank's Pest management policy 31 (OP4.09) would be invoked to develop and implement
ecologically based integrated pest management (IPM) strategies in all subprojects co-financed by the
Project in the agriculture sector where pest managementissues may have a potentially deleterious impact
on human health andenvironment.
The Project implementation team of Phase 1 has been successful in: (a) addressing procurement,
handling, application, and disposal of pest control products and monitoring the impact of pesticide use;
and (b) monitoring changes in agricultural practices and growing new crops and cultivars where
significantly different IPMmeasures were taken; particular attention was given to crops such as cotton,
vegetables, fruits, and rice, which are often associatedwith heavy use of pesticides (refer to Bank's policy
on OP 4.01, Annex C). Similar approacheswould be taken in the second phase but due to the scaling up
of the project nationwide additional attention will be given to train personnel inthe new regions about the
safeuse of pesticides and environmentally sound integrated pest managementprocedures.
A pest management planwas deemednecessarydue to Project interventions within Components 1and 2
that would: (i)  Change cultivation and management practices and use of newly improved cultivars and
crops that may have better pest tolerance; (ii)      Potential increased use of pesticide with agricultural
intensification; and (iii)Potentialuse of pesticides with introduced crops or cultivars in a geographic area
where it has not been cultivated previously.
The pest management plan inpreparation will address following issues:
(a) all subprojects receiving finance for procurement of pest control products from the Projec may be
used to purchase pest control products, the following products classified as "Class 1A and LB" and
specified "Class 2 formulations" usingguidelines of WHOPCS 200232;
(b) all subprojects receiving finance for procurement of pest control products directly or wil provide
credit that may be transporting, storing, or disposing environmentally significant and substantial
quantities of highly toxic pesticide materials for use under the Project will request a hazard assessment as
part of the subproject proposal indicating risk mitigation plan within the Environmental Plan (see section
A.10.2.);
(c) the Project in its subproject selection and monitoring would include financing for relevant support to
develop and implement an integrated pest management (IPM)program, aimed at reducing environmental
and health hazards associatedwith pest control and the use of pesticides;
(d) duringproject implementation, the Agricultural Specialist of the M&EUnitwith assistancefrom other
appropriate technical specialists would evaluate subproject proposals for their contribution to IPM
strategy, based on local conditions. Where there i s an identified need to strengthen the local capacity in
IPM,the national and internationalexpertise and available facilities of other institutes will be usedunder
a collaborative agreement with the Project; and
(e) the Project, to satisfy the requirements of the rules and regulations of the country, the IPM strategy of
the Project, and policy requirements of the Bank will establish collaboration with the Sewicio Nacional
de SunidadAgruria (SENASA), which i s the National Focal Point for the approval of pesticides for use in
Peru.




31Pestsincludeinsect pests, diseases, nematodes and other vertebrate pests.
32World HealthOrganization(WHOPCS). 2002 The WHO recommended Class$cation of Pesticidesby Hazard
and Guidelinesto Classification (Geneva:WHO, 2000-2002)


                                                      109

2. PEST MANAGEMENTACTION PLAN
Stage I: Includedinitial reconnaissanceto identify the main pest problems and their contexts (ecological,
agricultural, public health, economic, and institutional) and define broad parameters for evaluation at
Appraisal by the Component 2 with technical assistance from a Pest management specialist.
Stage ZI:      Development of specific operational plans to address the pest problems identified as a
component of the project itself. These activities may include and not be limited to:
(i)implementation and dissemination of the list of pest control products authorized for procurement (as
described earlier Class IA, IB and some Class I1formulations that are prohibited and the specified safe
products - Class I1onwards);
(ii)development of IPMapproaches (biological control, cultural practices in habitat management, use of
resistant or tolerant varieties, replacement of pesticide use to the minimum with other environmentally
safe practices) and generalpolicy compliance with the Bank's Policy OP4.09;
(iii) theProjectcomponent3activitiesandinrelationtotheEnvironmentalPlan,identifyactions
     within
required:     (a) to improve the policy, economic, institutional, and legal framework for regulating,
procuring, and managing pesticides that are consistent with an IPMapproach and are sustainable; and (b)
the proposed mechanisms for financing, implementing, monitoring, and supervising components relating
to pest management or pesticide use, including any role envisaged for the private sector including local
nongovernmental organizations;
(iv) depending on the nature and complexity of the pest management and pesticide-related issues
confirmed at appraisal, and in relation to the Environmental Plan, supervision missions may include
appropriate technical specialists inthe M&EPlan of the Project Component 3;
(v) establishment of a Training plan of the Project Component 2 to develop the capacity of subproject
partners and co-financers who are initiating extension, adaptive research, and strategic research
subprojects aimed at providing alternatives to undesirable pesticide use;
(vi) agreeing on a time-bound program to phase out the use of an undesirable pesticide and properly
dispose of any existing stocks, if applicable; and
(vii) at the end of the project, the Implementation Completion Report (ICR) would evaluate the
environmental impact of pest management practices supported or promoted by the project and the
borrower's institutional oversight capacity.

 in everything to do with the ecological strategy for pest management. The costs of this activity will be
 includedinthe activities of the INCAGRO follow-up andassessmentsystem (Project 3). It includes:
  1. Follow-up and assessment plan, specifying those responsible for its execution, the experts required by
    this plan, andthe costs involved.
 2. Determination of risk evaluation indicators, for evaluating potential environmental, occupational, and
     public health impacts associated with the transportation, storage, distribution, and use of the proposed
     products,under local conditions,andthe risks associatedwith the disposalof the containers.
 3. Guidelinesregardingpre-requisites and measures requiredfor reducingspecific risks associated with the
     use of pesticidestaken into accountby INCAGRO.
 4. Proposal of mechanisms for the financing, execution, follow-up, and supervision of the components
     associated with pest management or the use of pesticides, including preventive roles for the private
     sector; localnon-govemmentalorganizations are not excludedfrom playing such roles.
 5. INCAGRO, in its processes of selection and follow-up of subprojects will include assistance for the
     development and execution of integrated pest management (IPM) programs in order to reduce
     environmentalandhealthrisks associatedwith pestcontrolandthe useof pesticides.

                                         EXPOSICIOY DE MOTIVOS


               Esta Cai-ta de Politicas es la espresihii del coniproiniso del Gobierno del Peni con 10s
               objetivos de la Fase 11 (2005-2009) del Programa INCAGRO. La primera C'arta, dt.1 ;ifio
                1999, dio lugar al Acuerdo de Prestaino que financio una parte de la Fase [ del Progrnma. La
               presente Carta plantea 10s ajustrs que se estiman necesarios a la del atio 1999, incorporando
               la experiencia recogida durante la ejecucion de la Fase I,sefialando las lineas estrategicas
               para el fomento y desarrollo de un sistenia abierto y descentralizado de cicncia, tecnologia e
               innovation agraria, promoviendo 10s canibios institucionales necesarios y un us0 mas
               eficiente y equitativo de 10s recursos piblicos.

               Los logros obtenidos y el cumplimiento de 10s indicadores clave durante la F a x I,permiten
               que el Programa de Prestamo Ajustable (APL, por sus siglas en inglks) pueda continuar hacia
               su Fase 11. Actualmente, el Programa para la Fase I1 ya cuenta con la declaracion de
               viabilidad otorgada por el Ministerio de Economia y Finanzas al estudio de factibilidad. En
               consecuencia, para seguir el procedimiento establecido durante la Fase I,corresponde que la
               Carta de Politicas sea firmada por 10s Ministros de Agricultura y de Economia y Finanzas
               para permitir una adecuada negociacion de las condiciones del prestamo para la Fase 11, y
               garantizar, posteriormente, la firma del Acuerdo de Prestamo entre el Gobiemo del Penj y e l
               Banco Mundial.

               La Carta refuerza el objetivo central de politica agraria del Estado peruano. expresada en
               documentos oficiales del Sector, cual es el de elevar la rentabilidad y la competitividad del
               sector agrario, dinamizando el empleo y reduciendo la pobreza rural, en el marco del rol
               subsidiario del Estado, el us0 eficiente de 10s recursos publicos, e l manejo sostenible de 10s
               recursos naturales y la preservacion de la calidad del medio ambiente.

               Para alcanzar dicho objetivo, el Gobierno se propone continuar con el proceso de
               modemizacibn del sector, orientado a la construccibn de una plataforma de servicios, la cual
               permitira incrementar la competitividad de 10s productores agrarios, haciendo posible
               afrontar de manera eficiente 10s nuevos retos y oportunidades que se generaran como
               consecuencia del proceso de descentralizacion del pais, de la globalizaci6n y de 10s tratados
               de libre comercio.

               Enese marco, el objetivo de la Fase I1del Programa INCAGRO es contribuir a la expansion,

                agraria. La Carta hace explicit0 el rol del Estado en la modemizacibn institucional y de 10s

      adaptacion, difusi6n y us0 de tecnologias.

i provision. Hasta el momento, el Estado ha tenido un dkbil papel en promover y regular estos
  mercados y en algunos casos ha contribuido a distorsionar la asignacion de 10s escasos
  recursos disponibles.

   16. En este escenario, el reto para el Estado es contribuir al desarrollo de estos mercados,

   10s servicios para la innovacion.

 POLICY LETTERSUBMITTEDBY THE GOVERNMENTOF PERU(GOP)TO THE
                                               WORLDBANK

     REGARDINGPHASEI1OFTHE INCAGROPROGRAM:INNOVATIONAND
                        COMPETITIVENESSINAGRICULTUREINPERU


I. Introduction

1. This policy letter articulates the Government of Peru's commitment to the objectives of the
INCAGRO Program (Innovation and Competitiveness for Peruvian Agriculture). It addresses the
adjustments that need to be made to the 1999 Letter and the strategic guidelines for promoting and
developing an open and decentralized system for applying science, technology, and innovation in
agriculture, while fostering the institutional changes necessary, as well as the more efficient and equitable
use of public funds.

2.    The Peruvian Government's core agricultural policy objective i s to increase the profitability and
competitiveness of the agricultural sector, to promote employment and reduce poverty in rural areas, to
use public funds efficiently, and to manage natural resources and the environment in a sustainable
manner.

3.    To attain these objectives, the Government intends to forge ahead with the modernization of the
sector, focusing on building a services platform (technology, information, health, and land titling) to
support Peruvian farmers to be more competitive and thus be efficiently equipped to face the new
challenges and opportunities createdby globalization andfree trade agreements.

4.    Thus, as stated inFramework Law No. 28303 promulgated on July 23, 2004 on Science,
Technology, and Innovation, the Peruvian Government recognizes that the promotion and development of
science, technology, and technological innovation in agriculture are fundamental to increasing
productivity and enhancing national development in the various sectors. It i s also aware of the need to
take a medium and long-term approach to technological processes and hence plan them with a strategic
vision in mind. T h i s includes the institutional changes that are necessary as well as the more efficient use
of resources.

5.    Peru i s engaged in consolidating a process of decentralization, officially initiated in 2003, aimed
principally at promoting a more equitable distribution of economic wealth and social welfare, as well as a
more representative role of the regions in national government. These efforts will undoubtedly boost the
development of markets and new economic activity throughout the country, posing a new challenge for
the generation, tailoring, anddissemination of technology.

6.    Finally, the Peruvian Government acknowledges its responsibility for raisingthe standard of living
and opening up opportunities for citizens inthe most vulnerable sectors, such as the rural population. This
responsibility goes hand in hand with the need to foster, on a sustained basis, the ability of farmers to
have access to innovation services, and thus to markets. It i s for this reason that consideration should also
be given in the INCAGRO Phase I1program to investments designed to narrow technological gaps or to
mitigate processes that exclude specific population groups.


11. The Role of the Government in the Institutional Modernization of the System of Science,
      Technology, and Innovation inthe Agricultural Sector and Commitments of the Government


                                                       130

7.    The increased competitiveness of globalized markets calls for changes in the roles traditionally
assigned to the public and private sectors in technological development in agriculture. In agricultural
sector research, the following can be observed: a) an increasing diversity in terms of the institutions
involved, whereby in addition to traditional international and national public entities, new actors
are emerging such as academic institutions, businesses, non-governmental organizations and private
sector associations; b) a larger volume of public/private financing; c) increasing linkage with processes
of innovation that include such systems as quality control, biotechnological resources, intellectual
property rights, and patents, among others.

8.    This situation requires the Government to define its role and policies with respect to investment of
public funds in technological innovation, within a policy framework involving both the public and the
private sector in order to create the conditions for enhancing the rate of technological innovation in the
country. This framework must first recognize the many institutions involved in innovation and the
separation of institutional roles in order to address the three dimensions of the system: policy formulation,
financing, and the execution of activities.

9.    Inthat regard, the commitment of the Government is to support and monitor the process of change
necessary for modernization of the system of science, technology, and innovation, thereby creating the
public institutions that are specialized in the formulation and implementation of policies and priorities for
innovation as well as the financing of the system, while assigning public resources that support activities
inmany areas andthe decentralization of the execution of technologicalinnovationactivities.

10. Inthe context of this commitment, andwith a view to the separation of roles andthe modernization
of the sector, the Ministry of Agriculture will ensure that:

       a. The INCAGRO Program, through its financing mechanisms, contributes: i)to the sustainable
      development of a system of agricultural science technology, which i s plural, decentralized,
      demand-driven, and led by the private sector; ii)to the orientation of the necessary institutional
      changes, which will eventually lead to specialization of the roles mentioned above;

       b. The research institution established in the sector specializes in the performance of the research
      and the transfer of technology, thereby taking advantage of its comparative advantages derived
      from its presence in the different ecoregions of the country, in such a way that it concentrates its
      efforts, technical capacity, and financial resources on the execution of a sufficient number of
      prioritized programs and projects of strategic value, in which the nature of public funds i s
      recognized.


111. The Challenges Facing the Competitive Integration of Peruvian Agriculture into the Process
      of Globalization

11. The Peruvian agricultural sector is undergoingaprocessof transformationas it seeks to respondto
the dynamic global environment. This process should contribute to enhancing conditions that link small-
scale agriculture, which i s the predominant form of farming in Peru, to access to agroindustry and
national and internationalmarkets, inparticular inrelation to receipt by these farmers of a greater share of
the profit generated by agricultural activity, within a context of symmetrical and equitable relations
between the different actors inthe farming sector.




                                                       131

12, The sector's challenge is finding ways to compete in a marketing systemcharacterized by product
differentiation, where success is determined by the ability to develop competitive advantages that enable
national and internationaldemand for quality products to be met. These characteristics of the market have
increased the need for technology, no longer just in relation to the product itself, but also to the whole
production process, including sound agricultural practices, post-harvest handling and processing,
certification, labeling of origin, classification or standardization, packaging, food safety, and means of
storage andtransportation.

13. This is what makes technologies and processes based on know-how, and generated and
disseminated in a plural and decentralized science, technology and innovation system, so crucial, because
they will enable agriculture to react constructively to this challenge and take full advantage of the
potential benefits of multilateral and bilateral agreements, not just because of their direct impact in terms
of reducing production costs, enhancing productivity and competitiveness, but also because they afford
increased access to new markets and induce the creation and adaptation of new products, thereby
improving the chances of generating wealth for the country.

14. However, the highly fragmented ownership of the land and the absence of key markets (including
services for production, agribuisness markets, and technological innovation), have stymied the
development of a competitive agricultural sector. This i s evidenced by, among other things, sluggish
growth in agricultural and livestock productivity, scant capacity to generate employment, and the
problemstypical of rural areas today, above all, rural poverty.

15. In the case of the services market, the following is observed: a limited appreciation for and
capacity of many small farmers to pay for services due to low profit margins on their end-products, a lack
of experience of private providers in dealing with small farmers, difficulties of suppliers in gaining access
to the technical information and knowledge that permit them to maintain the quality of their supplies, and
the reluctance by private entities to provide services, a practice that leads to the perpetuation of
"subsidization" of provision of services. To date, the Government has played a largely ineffective role in
promoting and regulating such markets and in many cases has contributed to distortions in the allocation
of the scant resources available.

16. Against this backdrop, the challenge for the Government is to contribute to the development of
these markets through the promotion of specialized quality services, by subsidizing part of the transaction
costs which, at the moment, constitute a barrier to the efficient functioning of innovation services.


IV. The Objectives of the Long-TermProgramandthe Commitments of the Government

17. The long-term program serves as a frame of reference and provides the future vision in Peru in
order to improve the innovation and competitiveness of farming. The Program i s being gradually
implementedin the Ministry of Agriculture, with objectives and goals for each of the three phases: Phase
I,establishmentofadecentralizedsystemofinnovationinallthreeregions;Phase11,expansionofthe
system at the national level; Phase 111, consolidation of a plural system of science, technology, and
innovation, which i s decentralized, demand-driven, and ledby the private sector.

18. This Program is being partially financed with external resources borrowed from the APL
(Adaptable Loan Program) of the World Bank, with the commitment of the Peruvian Government to co-
finance eachphase incrementally.




                                                      132

19. The program's long-term objective i s to increase productivity and profitability, as well as enhance
the competitiveness of the agricultural sector by adopting sustainable and environmentally safe
technologies.

20. Inorder to contribute to the achievement of this objective, the Government of Peruundertakes to: a)
ensure the sustainability of the scientific and technological development of policies, using budgetary
allocations that match the needs of these policies; b) strengthen institutions and establish the necessary
institutional rules, while respecting specialization of roles and encouraging coordination among both
private and public actors; and c) invest in ongoing training and updating of the skills of human resources
and the infrastructure necessaryfor innovation.


V.    Achievements of the long-term program to date

21. At the turn of the century, the Government of Peru announced guidelines for a long-term program
fostering innovation and competitiveness inagriculture. That program, which gave rise to the Agricultural
Research and Extension Project (PEA) known as INCAGRO, was conceived as a three-phase program,
of 3, 4, and 5 years duration respectively, whereby the achievement of some trigger indicators in each
phase would be a precondition for the start of the nextphase.

22. The specific objectives of phase Iwere: a) to promote an efficient market for basic services that
expand knowledge and build human capacity and contribute directly to increasing technological
innovation and competitiveness in agriculture; and b) to support a number of institutions for capacity-
building, so that they can more effectively fulfill a strategic responsibility in the definition and
administration of a normative framework, which offer strategic services that correspond to the
Government.

23. With regard to the first specific objective, fourteen public bidding processes have been held to
award contracts, financed with FTA and FDSE funds, for 123 subprojects: 36 involving extension
services, 27 in adaptive research services, 28 in strategic research, 16 in extension support services
(training and information), and 16 in extension services for the pilot ("Huchuy Ayni" or small-scale
mutual assistance) in Huancavelica. The total amount awarded over the three years exceeds US$6.7
million, and involved a monetary and non-monetary co-financing commitment by strategic partners
(services operators and farmers' organizations) of nearly US$6.6 million. Over 100 operators are running
the subprojects, with the support and collaborationof more than 200 institutions.

24. Approximately 9,000 farmers are directly involved with the businessplans of the extension services
and adaptive research subprojects and another 1,500 are participating in strategic research, information,
and training. It i s estimated that at least another 30,000 farmers are benefiting from co-financed
subprojects and improved technology will be used in an area of at least 25,000 hectares.

25. Insofar as the second specific objective is concerned, the Program supported the preparation of the
strategic plan of the INIA (currently known as the INIEA). The evaluation indicates that the final plan
published by the INIA requires major efforts on the part of this institution to define the vision, mission,
and the strategic role that it must play in the context of a plural and decentralized technological
innovation system.

26. Some progress has been made with strategic research programs; for example with the genetic
resource programs and with biotechnology, animal and plant protection, and agricultural economics. In
the case of extension support programs (training and information), no progress has been made in terms of



                                                    133

the plans formulated, but experience and information have been acquired and promising programs
identified with the help of the FSDE.

27. Ingeneral terms, Phase Iof the Project has gained experience and has strengthened the position of
the Government in its financing of the system through its competitive funds, while encouraging a more
plural, decentralized, diversified, specialized, and co-financed dimension with respect to both financing
andthe provision of services for innovation, researchandtechnology development activities.


VI. The Proposalfor PhaseI1

28. The objective of Phase I1(2005-2009) of the INCAGRO Programis to contribute to the expansion,
strengthening, and institutional development of the agricultural science, technology, and technological
innovation system.

29. Thus, for Phase I1 of the Program, the Peruvian Government has undertaken to provide the
necessary counterpart funds to World Bank financing for the execution of this Program. It also undertakes
to make the appropriate institutional arrangements within its decentralized public entities and special
projects in order to synchronize its intervention strategies with the methods used by the Program in order
to avoid distortions and confusion among those requiring agricultural services inthe field.

30. Inaddition, once the mid-term evaluation indicates that Phase I1activities have been satisfactorily
achieved, the Government of Peru will make a commitment to issue a call for proposals from the entities
of the system, which will take place between 2008 and 2009, by providing 100% financing from its
budget funds which may be eligible for Phase I11 Loan financing. This will demonstrate both the
commitment of the Government to guarantee and replicate more widely the success achieved
with innovation and competitiveness inagriculture.

31. Building on the achievements mentioned above, and in line with the idea of expanding and
strengthening the plural, decentralized, demand-driven science, technology, and innovation system, ledby
the private sector, the objectives establishedfor Phase IIare to:

         a. Contribute to the decentralized development of the market for specialized services for
         agricultural innovation throughout the country by co-financing 188 sub-projects for extension
         services, 75 subprojects for adaptive research, and 330 training and technical assistance projects
         for the poor who require access to the services market. The funds to be earmarked for co-
         financing extension subprojects and adaptive research account for 86 percent of the total amount
         to be invested inthis objective, while the training and technical assistance subprojects account for
         14 percent. Through this subproject, it i s estimated that the needs of 46,000 organized farmers'
         who use the service will be met; As users of the services, farmers will provide US$5.72 million in
         co-financing, which, on average, represents30 percent of the total cost of subprojects.

         b. Increase support for at least six agricultural technology strategic programs, thereby
         contributing to the institutional reorientation towards centers for excellence in research and the
         co-financing of 48 projects for strategic research. Support will be provided for regional capacity
         building by co-financing 30 subprojects for training extension agents and 9 programs for
         providing incentives to researchers for sabbatical and post-graduate studies. It i s estimated that
         the co-financing of the executing entities of these 78 subprojects will amount to US$6.33 million.




                                                      134

        c. Foster strengthening of the system of science, technology, and agricultural innovation, and, in
        so doing, strengthen a system for monitoring and evaluation that identifies and recognizes
        best practices in the provision of services and innovative processes in the agricultural sector; and
        implement a system of scientific and technological information for the sector, as well as
        established priorities for that system.

        d. Contribute to the strengthening of the capacity to formulate policies to promote agricultural
        technologicalinnovation, within the framework of a modernizedMinistry of Agriculture.

32. Recognizingthe needto develop institutional capacities inorder to strengthen specialized entities in
every aspect of the agricultural science, technology, and innovation system, Phase I1seeks to integrate the
three technical projects of the Program, as an efficient management unit, with a flexible organizational
structure:



      Project 1. Strengthening the Innovation Services Market. The objective of this Project i s to
      move ahead with decentralized development of the market for specialized innovation services, by
      contributing to the strengthening and empowerment of farmers' organizations requiring services;
      fostering an entrepreneurial approach to the provision of quality services; and synchronizing the
      supply and demand for services so that the market can function efficiently. The Project will co-
      finance: a) usingcompetitive funds, extension services and adaptive research subprojects, based on
      business plans that reflect producer demands, including those meeting the demands of vulnerable
      groups, such as indigenous populations and women's organizations; b) local participatory groups,
      internships (prhcticas pre-profesionales), promotion and training workshops, and technical
      evaluation panels, all of which will be geared to enhancing farmers' organizational management
      skills and agribusiness capacities, as well as to boosting supplier capacities by fostering an
      entrepreneurial approach to the provision of services. INCAGRO will guarantee the participationof
      the technical representatives of the Regional Governments of the macroregions where activities
      related to this project are beingcarried out, particularly in connection with the use of competitive
      funds for aspects related to the publication, evaluation, and negotiation of subprojects. Inaddition,
      the use of the competitive funds will take decentralization factors into account, as well as their
      macroregional, regional, and local implications, with a view to strengthening the capacities of local
      players in the formulation and execution of technological innovation projects to enhance the
      competitiveness of regional agriculture.


      Project 2. Strategic Skills for Research and Development. The objective of this Project i s to
       strengthenresearchandtechnology development for agriculture inareas of the science, technology,
      and innovation system that are of national strategic importance, by helping to build institutional
       and professional skills. The Project should establish support mechanisms for: a) the strengthening
       of centers of excellence in emerging areas of science and technology and b) the establishment
       of regional programs offering training in high-skill innovation services, which are vital for
       increasing agricultural competitiveness. The Project will administer a competitive fund which will
      finance: a) sound national and international strategic partnerships for co-financing the development
       of researchcapacities and activities, initially inthree priority areas: conservation and use of genetic
      resources, biotechnology, and integrated protection of plants and livestock products, and then
       gradually accompanied by three new priority programs - natural resource management (including
       soil and land management, water management and irrigation, and agroforestry), post-harvest
       handling and processing, and conservation agriculture; b) capacity-building of public research
       institutions in order to co-finance research activities that are of strategic value, in which the nature



                                                      135

      of public funds is recognized and integrated into a strategic research program for small-scale
      agriculture; c) regional extension worker training programs to co-finance curricular programs
      focusing on skills and institutional development; and d) incentive programs for researchers at
      national and regional centers, which co-finance post-graduate and sabbatical professional training
      fellowships in special fields within strategic research priority areas that require a professional
      critical mass inline with institutional development.

      Project 3. Policies, Information, and Quality of Innovation Services. The objective of this
     .Project i s to buildcapacity in the public sector to formulate and implement innovation indquality-
      related policies for a plural, decentralized, and demand-driven modern system of science,
      technology, and agricultural innovation. The result should be the building of capacity within the
      Ministry of Agriculture in order to determine policies and coordinate investment with the private
      sector, with a focal point being identified within the Ministry of Agriculture. This objective will be
      the result o f a) the establishment of an institutional framework for the procedures, priorities, and
      policies for the promotion and protection of innovation which are widely accepted within the
      system; b) the ongoing improvement of the processes and results of the activities related to
      technological innovation and social control in the use of resources; c) the availability and use of
      scientific and technological innovation in the activities and decisions related to agricultural
      innovation. The Project will: a) finance studies and events related to prospective technology,
      specify innovation priorities and policies, and define new strategic research areas; b) monitor and
      evaluate the subprojects that are co-financed, within the framework of the National Public
      Investment System by preparing standardization indicators and developing mechanisms for
      the recognition of best practices related to innovation and competitiveness; c) finance the
      implementation of a scientific and technological information platform for the system.

      Organization. In order to guarantee plurality, decentralization, and the participation of the
      different players in the system at the national level, the Program will be directed by an Executive
      Board, which, for management purposes, will be composed of specialized committees. At the
      regional level, the Programwill have Macroregional ConsultativeCouncils (CCMs).

      The Executive Board will be chaired by the Minister of Agriculture and will be composed of 9
      members. These persons will have a genuine interest in promoting the objectives of the Program,
      will be prominent citizens whose prestige and experience are recognized, and will truly represent
      the scientific, business, social, and environmental spheres, and possess experience in formulating
      policies that foster technological innovation.

      The Program Management Unit (PMU), whose function i s to administer and finance the Program,
      inaccordancewith acceptedtechnical, economic and financial, social, and environmental processes
      and procedures, will be composed of an Executive Directorate and four units, three of which will
      be technical, and the other, administrative. It will have eight decentralized units, which, in turn,
      will be supported by the same number of Macroregional Consultative Councils (CCMs).


VII. The triggers for Phase I11of the Program

33. The triggersfor Phase I11will be basedon the findings of an external review. These triggers are: a)
establishment of a focal point for policies to support agricultural technological innovation within the
Ministry of Agriculture, responsible for regulation, establishment of priorities, the channeling of public
financing, and a suitable framework for the recognition of intellectual property rights; b) the positive
evaluation of the formulation and implementation of actions plans by the CCMs, with the participation of
the representativesof Regional Governments, development institutions, and farmers' organizations; c) the


                                                     136

positive evaluation of the competitive funds of Project Iin all regions, with the satisfactory performance
of at least 75 percent of the subprojects assigned; d) the positive evaluation of at least three of the
strategic programs financed by Project 2; e) verification that the strategic partnerships are co-financed
with monetary resources that amount to at least 30 percent and 10 percent of the cost of the subprojects
assignedby Project 1and Project 2, respectively.


VIII. PhaseI11of the Program

34. During Phase I11of the Program, the Government will consolidate a decentralized, plural, and co-
financed system of science, technology, and agricultural innovation, with public and private financing
assistance.

35. To attain this objective, the investment made by the Government in the system will have led to the
specialization of institutionalroles and to the strengthenedperformance of both the players in the services
markets as well as the research and technology centers for excellence. This will position the system to
implement an agenda that i s in keeping with the ongoing challenges of globalization and social needs,
thereby permitting the more efficient use of the resources that are invested by the Government in the
system, channelingthem towards highstakes public issues.

36. Because of the need to improve and maintain agricultural competitiveness in economies that are
becoming increasingly open, both public and private investment must be increased on a sustained basis
well beyond the end of the Program.

37. To that end, and as a result of the Program, the system will have plural and decentralized
institutions and an appropriate policy and regulatory framework, which will pave the way for efficient use
of the resources of both the public and private sectors. Inthat context, the commitment of the Government
will be to keep investment levels inline with its responsibilities.

Lima, February 16,2005.




            Alvaro Enrique QuijandriaSalmbn                    Pedro Pablo Kuczynski Godard
                   Minister of Agriculture                    Minister of Economy and Finance
